Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Bibliography of a Critical Edition
Bibliography of sources for a critical edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of a bibliography in a critical edition and distinguish between primary and secondary sources used in editing Hanafi fiqh texts.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the scholarly rigor behind the text you study.

When you open a critical edition of a classical Hanafi text like Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, you often find a list of sources. This is not just a formality—it is a roadmap of the editor's research. This lesson helps you read that list intelligently, understanding which works are foundational for the Hanafi madhhab and how the editor has used them to establish a reliable text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scope
Look at the range of disciplines covered. This list includes biography, fiqh, history, weights and measures, and pilgrimage rites. Consider why an editor would need all these for a fiqh commentary.
A thorough edition cross-references many fields to ensure accuracy.
2
Classify the Sources
Separate primary Hanafi fiqh sources (e.g., Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Bada'i' al-Sana'i') from secondary references (e.g., biographical dictionaries, historical works like I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in).
Primary sources are directly on fiqh; secondary sources provide context and verification.
3
Note Publication Details
Observe that many entries list modern critical editions and editors. This tells you the editor relied on established scholarly work, not just old prints.
Modern editions often include corrections and additional commentary.
4
Recognize Authority
Some works are by later Hanafi authorities like Ibn Nujaym and Ibn Abidin. Their presence indicates that the commentator (al-Quduri) is being interpreted through the later tradition.
The hierarchy of Hanafi texts is important: earlier matn, later sharh.
5
Apply to Your Study
Use this bibliography as a reading list for deepening your understanding of the madhhab. For example, start with Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq for a comprehensive commentary.
Knowing these sources helps you navigate the Hanafi fiqh tradition.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography of sources used by the editor (Sā’id Bakdāsh) in preparing the critical edition of Al-Lubāb Sharḥ al-Qudūrī. It lists 35 works (entries 21-35) spanning multiple Islamic disciplines: biography, jurisprudence, ḥadīth, history, weights and measures, and pilgrimage rites. Many are foundational Hanafi texts (e.g., Al-Bahr al-Rā’iq, Bada’i‘ al-Ṣanā’i‘) or key references for understanding the madhhab. The editor has drawn on both classical and modern scholarly editions to ensure accuracy. This list demonstrates the rigorous textual methodology employed in producing the edition, which is essential for students who rely on the text's authority.

Key Terms
تحقيق (taḥqīq): Critical editing of a classical text, involving comparison of manuscripts and scholarly verification.
متن (matn): The base text that is being commented upon, e.g., Al-Quduri's matn.
شرح (sharḥ): Commentary that explains and expands on the matn, e.g., Al-Lubab is a sharh of Al-Quduri.
محقق (muḥaqqiq): The person who performs taḥqīq (critical edition), e.g., Sa'id Bakdash for this work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The bibliography of a critical edition is a key to understanding the editor's method and the scholarly tradition of the text.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Understanding the Scholarly Apparatus: Sources of a Critical Edition
Bibliography of reference works used in the critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Hanafi reference works from a critical edition's bibliography and explain their importance in fiqh research.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the textual foundation of a Hanafi fiqh work.

This passage is not a fiqh ruling but a list of sources used to verify and edit the text of al-Quduri and its commentary al-Lubab. Understanding such bibliographies is crucial for any serious student of Hanafi fiqh, as it teaches you which works are authoritative, how scholars depend on each other, and how to trace a fiqh ruling back to its original source. In this lesson, we will examine the first few entries of this bibliography to understand the landscape of Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genre of each source
Look at the titles: are they fiqh commentaries, hadith collections, biographical works, etc.? This helps you understand the type of authority each source carries.
For example, al-Bahr al-Raiq is a fiqh commentary, while Bughyat al-Wu'at is a biographical dictionary.
2
Note the author and his death date
The death date (t) places the work in a historical context. Earlier works are often more foundational; later works may be commentaries or compilations.
Al-Kasani (d. 587 AH) is earlier than Ibn Nujaym (d. 970 AH).
3
Identify the relationship to Hanafi fiqh
Determine which works are directly about Hanafi law (e.g., Bada'i' al-Sana'i', al-Bahr al-Raiq) versus works from other disciplines like hadith or language.
This helps you prioritize sources when researching a fiqh ruling.
4
Trace the chain of commentary
Notice how al-Binayah is a commentary on al-Hidayah, which is itself a commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi. This reveals the intertextual dependence of Hanafi works.
Such chains show the development of Hanafi fiqh through generations.
5
Assess the modern edition details
Publisher, edition number, and year allow you to evaluate the reliability of the edition used. Multiple editions or manuscript references indicate a thorough editorial process.
Entry 36 lists both a printed edition and a manuscript, showing the editor used multiple witnesses.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography listing the reference works used by the editor (Muhaqqiq) in producing the critical edition of the two Hanafi texts: al-Quduri and its commentary al-Lubab. The list includes sources numbered 30 to 43, covering works of Hanafi fiqh, Hadith, biographical dictionaries, and other auxiliary sciences. The editor has carefully cited each work with its author, date of death, publication details, and edition information. This type of front matter is common in scholarly editions to establish the textual authority of the sources consulted. The user of this edition can trace any citation back to its original source through this list. For students, this list serves as a window into the scholarly apparatus behind the printed text rather than a fiqh lesson.

Key Terms
مصادر تحقيق (masādir taḥqīq): Sources used by the critical editor to establish the text
اللباب (al-lubāb): A Hanafi fiqh commentary on al-Quduri by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
الهداية (al-Hidāyah): A seminal Hanafi fiqh work by al-Marghinani, a commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi.

Key Takeaway
A critical edition's bibliography is a roadmap to the sources of Hanafi fiqh; learning to read it equips you to evaluate the authority of any ruling.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Editor's Bibliography: A Window into Hanafi Scholarly Sources
List of reference works used by the editor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the types of sources (biographical, historical, fiqh, linguistic) used in a critical edition of a Hanafi text and explain the contribution of each type to textual criticism.

Core Idea
A critical edition is only as strong as its sources — this bibliography reveals the depth and breadth of Hanafi scholarship.

When a scholar prepares a critical edition of a classical fiqh text like Al-Lubāb Sharḥ al-Qudūrī, they do not simply reprint an old manuscript. They consult dozens of works across multiple disciplines to verify attributions, clarify terms, and contextualize rulings. This list from the editor's introduction gives us a glimpse into that painstaking process. Understanding these source types helps you appreciate how modern scholarship reconstructs and preserves the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the purpose of the list
The list is titled 'Sources for the edition of Al-Lubab and Al-Quduri' (مصادر تحقيق اللباب والقدوري). It is a bibliography of reference works consulted by the editor. It is not a fiqh ruling or a lesson in itself.
This is front matter — it helps you evaluate the reliability of the edition.
2
Categorize each entry by genre
Go through the entries and sort them into categories: biographical works (Taj al-Tarajim, Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya), general histories (Tarikh al-Islam, Tarikh Baghdad), linguistic works (Taj al-ʿArus), and fiqh commentaries (Tabin al-Haqaʾiq, al-Bahr al-Raʾiq).
Many works span multiple categories, but identify their primary focus.
3
Note the chronological and geographical range
The sources range from the 5th century Hijri (al-Quduri himself, d. 428) to the 14th century (al-Kawthari, d. 1371). They originate from diverse regions: Damascus, Baghdad, Cairo, Kuwait, and more. This demonstrates the international and multi-century scope of Hanafi scholarship.
A critical edition must draw from both early and late sources to trace the textual tradition.
4
Understand why each genre is necessary
Biographical works help identify authors and verify chains of transmission. Histories provide context for dating manuscripts and events. Linguistic works aid in explaining rare terms. Earlier fiqh commentaries help reconstruct the text and resolve variants.
For example, the editor may have used Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya to confirm a ruling's attribution.
5
Apply the concept to a hypothetical scenario
Imagine the editor finds a questionable phrase in a manuscript of al-Quduri's text. How could entries like 'Taj al-Tarajim' or 'Tabin al-Haqaʾiq' help?
Biographies might date the scribe; commentaries might quote the text in a reliable form.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography, specifically a list of sources used by the editor of this edition of al-Lubāb Sharḥ al-Qudūrī. The list covers biographical works like Tāj al-Tarājim and Tabaqāt al-Ḥanafiyyah, lexicons like Tāj al-ʿArūs, histories like those by Brockelmann and al-Dhahabī, and important Hanafi fiqh commentaries such as Tabīn al-Ḥaqāʾiq and the supplement to al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq. Also listed is al-Tajrīd by al-Qudūrī himself on points of dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is, and works by later scholars like Ibn ʿĀbidīn and al-Kawtharī. This demonstrates the depth of the editor's research, drawing from early and late sources, across disciplines like biography, language, history, and fiqh. The inclusion of both printed editions and manuscripts (where noted) reflects scholarly standards.

Key Terms
مصادر التحقيق (maṣādir al-taḥqīq): The sources used by the editor of a critical edition; referring to the list of reference works on pages 507-508.
اللباب (al-lubāb): A Hanafi fiqh commentary by ʿAbd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī (d. 1298H) on al-Qudūrī's Mukhtaṣar.
القدوري (al-qudūrī): Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad al-Qudūrī (d. 428H), author of the famous Hanafi fiqh manual al-Mukhtaṣar.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Reading a Hanafi Tahqiq Bibliography: The Sources Behind al-Lubab
Bibliography of sources for the critical edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of sources listed in a Hanafi tahqiq bibliography and explain their role in verifying a classical fiqh text.

Core Idea
A tahqiq bibliography is a window into the scholarly apparatus that authenticates a fiqh text; each source is a building block in the chain of transmission.

When you open a critical edition of a Hanafi fiqh work like al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, you may encounter pages of bibliography. These lists are not mere decoration; they are the editor's toolkit for establishing the correct text and its meaning. This lesson walks you through the sources cited on pages 509-510 of the edition, showing you how to read such a list and what each category of source contributes to the study of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the purpose of a tahqiq bibliography
Understand that the bibliography documents the sources the editor used to establish the correct text, including manuscripts and earlier printed editions. It serves as a scholarly warrant for the edition's accuracy.
The title 'مصادر تحقيق اللباب والقدوري' explicitly states this purpose.
2
Identify different categories of sources
Categorize each cited work: Hanafi commentaries (e.g., Tuhfat al-Fuqaha', Tashih al-Quduri), hadith collections and takhrij works (e.g., Tuhfat al-Muhtaj, al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib), tafsir (e.g., Tafsir Ibn Kathir, Tafsir al-Jalalayn), biographical works (e.g., Tadhkirat al-Huffaz), and medical treatises (e.g., Tadhkirat Uli al-Albab).
Note that some works, like the medical treatise, may seem tangential but were used for specific rulings (e.g., on siwak).
3
Note the significance of manuscript references
Observe that some entries cite manuscripts (e.g., Tarajim Shuyukh al-Khulasi, Ta'tir al-Masham). This indicates the editor consulted unpublished sources, adding unique value to the edition.
Manuscripts are often the most authoritative witnesses for the text.
4
Consider the geographical and temporal distribution
Notice scholars from different regions (Samarqand, Egypt, Aleppo) and eras (6th-14th centuries AH). This shows the broad reliance on the Hanafi tradition across time and space.
The inclusion of later commentators like al-Laknawi (d. 1304 AH) shows the living tradition of Hanafi scholarship.
5
Relate the bibliography to your own study
Use this list as a starting point for locating additional sources to deepen your understanding of a particular fiqh issue. For example, al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib can help verify hadiths cited in al-Quduri.
A good tahqiq edition is a gateway to the broader scholarly literature.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography section from the critical edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, listing the sources consulted by the editor for the verification (tahqiq) of the text. It includes works by Hanafi scholars such as al-Samarqandi, al-Laknawi, Ibn al-Mulaqqin, and Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, as well as general reference works like Tafsir al-Jalalayn and Tadhkirat al-Huffaz. The list is numbered from 59 to 74, indicating a comprehensive collection of primary and secondary sources. The editor mentions multiple editions and manuscripts for some works, showing the scholarly methodology of collation. This section is not part of the original fiqh text but is essential for understanding the critical apparatus of the edition.

Key Terms
تحقيق (tahqiq): In this context, the critical editing and verification of a classical text by comparing manuscripts and citing sources.
مصادر (masadir): Sources; the list of references used by the editor in the critical edition.
مخطوط (makh tut): Manuscript; a handwritten copy of a work, often the most authoritative witness for textual criticism.
طبعة (tab'a): Edition or printing; indicates a published version of a work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A tahqiq bibliography is an essential scholarly tool that maps the textual and interpretive lineage of a fiqh work.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Understanding the Scholarly Apparatus: Hanafi Fiqh Bibliography
Listing of references used in the edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of sources (manuscripts, printed editions, commentaries) listed in a Hanafi fiqh bibliography and explain their role in textual criticism.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the chain of transmission and scholarly engagement with a foundational Hanafi text.

This passage is a bibliography from the critical edition of al-Lubab, a commentary on al-Quduri. At first glance, it may look like a dry list of titles and publication details. But for a Hanafi jurist, this list is a treasure map. It shows which manuscripts survived, which scholars commented on the text, and how the tradition was transmitted. In this lesson, you will learn to read such a bibliography as evidence of the living Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Scan for repeated names
Look for names like Qasim ibn Qutlubugha and Ibn Abidin. They appear multiple times. What does that tell you about their importance?
2
Distinguish manuscripts from printed works
Note which entries have '(مخطوط)'. Why would a critical edition rely on manuscripts?
3
Identify the types of works
Are they commentaries, supercommentaries, hadith collections, fatwa collections? Sort them.
4
Trace the chain of commentary
Notice entries that are commentaries on al-Quduri (e.g., Tashih al-Quduri, Takmilat al-Quduri). How do they relate to each other?
5
Consider the chronological range
The authors span from the 6th to the 14th century AH. What does that indicate about the ongoing relevance of al-Quduri's text?

Commentary
This is a bibliography section from the critical edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It lists the primary sources (manuscripts and printed works) used by the editor to establish the text. The list includes works directly on al-Quduri (like At-Tashil ad-Daruri and Tashih al-Quduri), commentary traditions (like Takmilat al-Quduri and Taqrib al-Gharib), and auxiliary texts (like Tafsir al-Jalalayn and At-Targhib wa at-Tarhib). Many entries refer to manuscripts, indicated by '(مخطوط)', highlighting the reliance on handwritten copies. The editor also references later Hanafi fatwa collections (Taqrirat ar-Rafi'i, Hashiyat Ibn 'Abidin) and Hadith works (Sunan at-Tirmidhi). This bibliography serves as a scholarly apparatus, documenting the textual basis for the edition.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): A commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar by al-Maydani, the main text of this edition.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
مخطوط (makhtut): Manuscript; indicates that the source exists only in handwritten form, not printed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A critical edition's bibliography is not just a reading list; it is a primary source for understanding the history of Hanafi scholarship and the textual transmission of its foundational works.

Key Sources in the Edition of Lubab and Quduri
Bibliography of sources for the critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi fiqh works referenced in the critical edition of Lubab Sharh al-Quduri and state their authors and significance.

Core Idea
The bibliography of the edition reveals the foundational texts of the Hanafi school.

This lesson introduces you to the scholarly references that underpin the critical edition of al-Lubab (the commentary on al-Quduri's matn). These sources include essential Hanafi fiqh works, hadith collections, tafsirs, and biographical dictionaries. Understanding these references helps you appreciate the depth of Hanafi scholarship and locate primary texts for your own research.

Guided Path
1
List the works cited
Scan the source list from entry 83 to 97. Write down the title of each work and its author as given.
Some entries like 'Hashiyat Ibn 'Abidin' are referenced indirectly.
2
Classify by genre
For each work, determine its genre: Hanafi fiqh, hadith, tafsir, biography, or methodology.
For example, 'Jami' al-Usul' is a hadith work, while 'Tanwir al-Absar' is a Hanafi fiqh text.
3
Identify Hanafi fiqh works
From the list, select only those that are directly Hanafi fiqh texts, such as Tanwir al-Absar, Jami' al-Rumuz, or Tahdhib al-Asma'.
Tahdhib al-Asma' is a biographical work that helps identify names in al-Hidayah; it is a tool for Hanafi study.
4
Connect to the edition
Consider how each source contributes to the critical edition of Lubab: e.g., Tanwir al-Absar is the base for Ibn 'Abidin's Hashiyah, which is used for commentary; Jami' al-Bayan provides tafsir for Qur'anic verses cited in the text.
The edition's editor used these to verify quotations and provide annotations.

Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This is a bibliography section listing sources used in the critical edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It includes references to major Hanafi works like Tanwir al-Absar wa Jami' al-Bihar by al-Timurtashi (which is the basis of Ibn 'Abidin's Hashiyah), and other essential texts such as Tahdhib al-Asma' al-Waqi'ah fi al-Hidayah wa al-Khulasah, which aids in identifying names found in al-Hidayah. The list also covers hadith works like Jami' al-Usul and Tahdhib al-Mustadrak, Qur'anic tafsirs such as Jami' al-Bayan and Jami' li Ahkam al-Qur'an, and biographical and methodological works. Each entry provides the author's name, death date, editor, publisher, and edition. This serves as a reference for students and researchers working with the edition of Lubab and Quduri.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): A Hanafi fiqh text (matn) by al-Quduri; Lubab is the commentary by al-Maydani.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), author of the Matn al-Quduri in Hanafi fiqh.
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical edition; scholarly editing of a manuscript with notes and sources.
تنوير الأبصار (Tanwir al-Absar): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Timurtashi, which is the basis of Ibn 'Abidin's famous hashiah.
جامع الرموز (Jami' al-Rumuz): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah by al-Qahistani, a Hanafi fiqh work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which work is the basis of Ibn 'Abidin's famous Hashiyah?
A) Tanwir al-Absar wa Jami' al-Bihar
B) Tahdhib al-Asma'
C) Jami' al-Usul
D) al-Jami' al-Saghir

Key Takeaway
The critical edition of Lubab relies on a wide range of Hanafi, hadith, and tafsir sources, reflecting the interdisciplinary nature of Hanafi scholarship.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Role of Bibliographies in Hanafi Fiqh Editions
List of sources for textual verification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of sources listed in a classical Hanafi fiqh bibliography and explain their function in textual verification.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography is the backbone of textual trust — manuscripts anchor the chain.

This lesson examines the bibliography (qā'imat al-maṣādir) appended to the critical edition of al-Lubāb Sharḥ al-Qudūrī by al-Maydānī. Such lists are not mere afterthoughts; they are the editor's attestation of the sources used to reconstruct the text. Understanding these lists allows you to assess the reliability of an edition and trace the transmission of Ḥanafī works.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish manuscript vs. printed source
Identify which entries are manuscripts (مخطوط) and which are printed works. In this list, entries 99, 101, and possibly 100 (partly manuscript) are marked or described as manuscripts.
2
Identify the genre of each work
Categorize each entry into fields like ḥadīth, tafsīr, fiqh, ṭabaqāt, or thabāt (licenses). For example, no. 91 is a thabāt, no. 92 is a ḥadīth collection, no. 93 is a tafsīr.
3
Recognize the chain of authority
Note the centuries of the authors: early sources like al-Ṭabarī (d. 310) and later ones like al-Nābulusī (d. 1143). This shows the editor's range.
4
Assess the edition's methodology
Observe that the editor uses both primary manuscripts (e.g., al-Kadūrī's commentary) and standard printed works. This indicates a thorough approach.
5
Understand the purpose: textual verification
Each source provides evidence for reconstructing the correct text of al-Lubāb and al-Qudūrī. For instance, a ḥadīth collection may verify a prophetic report cited in the text.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (qā'imat al-maṣādir) of works used by the editor in verifying the text of al-Lubāb and al-Qudūrī. It lists 13 entries (numbered 91–103) comprising manuscripts and printed books, including ḥadīth collections, Qur'ānic commentaries, Ḥanafī fiqh works, biographical dictionaries, and licenses (thabāt). The list emphasises authoritative sources in the Ḥanafī tradition, such as works by al-Ṭaḥāwī, al-Qudūrī, and later commentators. The presence of manuscripts indicates the editor's reliance on primary sources. This section is typical of critical editions and serves as a reference for verifying the authenticity of transmitted texts.

Key Terms
مخطوط (makhṭūṭ): A handwritten manuscript, as distinguished from a printed book. In this bibliography, entries 99, 101, and part of 100 are manuscripts.
ثبت (thabat): A register of a scholar's teachers, works, and licenses (ijazat). Entry 91 is a thabat of al-Kuzbari.
طبقات الحنفية (ṭabaqāt al-ḥanafiyya): Biographical dictionary of Hanafi scholars. Entry 102 is al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya, a major work in this genre.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Manuscripts are cheaper to reproduce than printed books.

Key Takeaway
A bibliography in a critical edition is not a formality; it is the backbone of textual verification, linking the printed text to its manuscript and printed sources.

Introduction and Front Matter

Parsing the Bibliography of a Hanafi Critical Edition
List of reference works cited by the editor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of sources (printed vs manuscript, primary vs secondary) listed in a Hanafi critical edition bibliography and evaluate their relevance to the study of al-Quduri.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the scholarly apparatus behind the text—manuscripts, commentaries, and supporting works.

This passage is a list of references from the editor's introduction to al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It is not a legal text but a critical tool. Understanding how to parse such a bibliography helps you locate primary Hanafi sources and gauge the editor's methodology.

Guided Path
1
Scan Entry Numbers
Check the range of entries (119–134) and count them. Verify continuity—are any numbers missing? This ensures you have the complete list.
Entries 119–134 = 16 sources. No gaps in this excerpt.
2
Categorize by Genre
Read each title and classify the work's subject: tafsir (e.g., Hashiyat Qurrat al-Aynayn), fiqh (e.g., Al-Hujjah 'ala Ahl al-Madinah), history (e.g., Hilyat al-Bashar), or fiqh rulings (e.g., Hukm Akhdh al-Sha'r).
Many entries are fiqh works relevant to Hanafi jurisprudence.
3
Identify Manuscript vs Printed
Look for the word 'مخطوط' (manuscript) or the absence of a publisher. For example, entry 122 is a manuscript; entry 121 is a printed book. This tells you about accessibility.
Manuscripts indicate the editor consulted original copies; printed books are more widely available.
4
Trace the Hanafi Connection
Note authors known to be Hanafi: al-Shaybani (entry 121), Mulla 'Ali al-Qari (124), al-Khassaf (131), Abu Yusuf (132). Their works are primary sources for Hanafi fiqh.
This shows the editor relied on the core Hanafi tradition.
5
Evaluate Editorial Significance
Consider why each source appears. Some are direct commentaries on al-Quduri (e.g., Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri, entry 128), others provide context or alternative rulings.
A well-chosen bibliography supports the critical apparatus of the edition.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (list of sources) from the critical edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It appears at the end of the book's introduction, listing the references consulted by the editor, Prof. Dr. Sa'id Bakdash. The entries range from number 119 to 134, covering works on tafsir, Hadith, fiqh, history, and language. Many are well-known Hanafi works, such as al-Hujjah 'ala Ahl al-Madinah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, and commentaries on al-Quduri. The editor includes both printed books and manuscripts. This list serves to document the scholarly apparatus behind the edition. Since it is front matter, no legal rulings are stated; rather, it provides transparency about the sources used.

Key Terms
مخطوط (makhṭūṭ): Manuscript: a handwritten copy, as opposed to a printed book. In bibliography, it indicates the work exists only in manuscript form.
شرح (sharḥ): Commentary: an explanation of a base text. Here, 'Sharh al-Quduri' is a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
طبعة حجرية (ṭabʿat ḥajariyyah): Lithograph edition: a printing method using stone plates, common in India. Entry 127 is a lithograph.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) 131 - Al-Hiyal

Key Takeaway
The bibliography in a critical edition is a roadmap to the sources used; learning to parse it is essential for serious Hanafi scholarship.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Hanafi Bibliography of Al-Lubab
Bibliography of sources for a Hanafi fiqh commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify at least three major Hanafi fiqh reference works listed in the bibliography of al-Lubab and state their authors.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the scholarly lineage that supports a classical fiqh text.

This passage is the bibliography (مصادر تحقيق) from the critical edition of al-Lubab, the Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It lists sources used by the editor for verification and commentary. While it contains no legal rulings, understanding these sources helps you appreciate the broader Hanafi textual tradition and the tools scholars use to ensure accuracy. This lesson will guide you through recognizing key works, their authors, and their relevance.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list and note titles
Read through the entries from 135 to 151. Identify each title in Arabic and its transliteration. Focus on works you have encountered before, like al-Durr al-Mukhtar or Durar al-Hukkam.
Titles often begin with 'al-' and include genre words like 'Sharh' (commentary) or 'Takhrij' (hadith verification).
2
Identify authors and death dates
For each entry, note the author's name and his death date (e.g., al-Haskafi d. 1088 AH). This helps you place the work in the Hanafi scholarly timeline.
Death dates are given after 'ت' (ta' marbuta).
3
Categorize each work
Group the entries by genre: Hanafi fiqh (e.g., al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Durar al-Hukkam), hadith (al-Diraya, al-Zawa'id), biographical (Khulasat al-Athar, al-Durar al-Kamina), or other.
Some works serve multiple purposes, like al-Durr al-Manthur (tafsir).
4
Highlight directly relevant Hanafi works
Identify which works are directly used in Hanafi fiqh study. For example, al-Durr al-Mukhtar is a major late Hanafi text, and Khulasat al-Dala'il is a commentary on al-Quduri.
These are the core texts you might consult for detailed rulings.
5
Understand the value of bibliography
Realize that such a list shows the scholarly apparatus behind a critical edition. It allows you to verify sources, trace citations, and assess the reliability of the edition.
For a student, knowing these sources enables deeper research and critical reading.

Commentary
This passage is the bibliography (مصادر تحقيق) of the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri. It lists the sources consulted by the editor(s) for verification and commentary. The list includes works on Hanafi fiqh (like Khulasat al-Dala'il, Durar al-Hukkam, al-Durr al-Mukhtar), hadith (al-Diraya, al-Zawa'id), biographical dictionaries (Khulasat al-Athar, al-Durar al-Kamina, Rawd al-Bashar), and other reference works. The entries give author, death date, publisher, and edition. This section shows the scholarly apparatus of the edition and is not a fiqh lesson. Students should note that this is a front-matter list and does not contain legal rulings.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): Title of the commentary (Sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Maydani.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
الدر المختار (al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A late Hanafi fiqh work by al-Haskafi, often glossed by Ibn Abidin.
درر الحكام (Durar al-Hukkam): A Hanafi legal work by Mulla Khusraw, with a commentary Ghurar al-Ahkam.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Hanafi Scholarly Chain: A Bibliography of Key Commentaries
Bibliography of sources for a critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Mukhtasar al-Tahawi from the bibliography and explain their role in preserving the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Knowing the sources is fiqh literacy — the chain of commentaries preserves the madhhab.

This passage is a bibliography from the critical edition of Al-Lubab (the commentary) and its base text, Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It lists manuscripts and printed works used to establish a reliable text. For the student of Hanafi fiqh, understanding these sources reveals how the tradition was transmitted, refined, and verified over centuries. The list includes early authorities like al-Jassas and al-Tahawi, and later commentators like al-Laknawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base texts
The bibliography revolves around two foundational matns: Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) and Mukhtasar al-Tahawi by Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH). Note that both are abridged works (mukhtasarat) that became core curricula in Hanafi madrasas.
Al-Quduri's text is the matn of the present edition; Al-Lubab is a commentary on it.
2
Recognize the commentary tradition
Each entry is a sharh (commentary) on one of these matns. Track the centuries: e.g., al-Jassas (d. 370 AH) on Tahawi, al-Uzjandi (6th c. AH) on Quduri, and later commentators like al-Fanari (d. 839 AH). This shows the continuous engagement of Hanafi scholars with the core texts.
Commentaries often include multiple layers: matn, sharh, and hashiyah (gloss).
3
Differentiate manuscript vs. printed
Many entries are marked (مخطوط) — manuscript. For example, the commentaries by al-Uzjandi, Khuwahar Zada, Ibn Danishmand, al-Fanari, and al-Samarqandi are all manuscripts. This indicates that not all scholarly works have been published; some remain in libraries, requiring direct access for verification.
Printed works (e.g., al-Dardir's Sharh al-Kabir) are more accessible but may have later additions.
4
Note the editorial team
The edition was prepared by prominent 20th-century Hanafi scholars: Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, and Dr. Abd al-Sattar Abu Ghuddah. Their involvement ensures that the edition meets scholarly standards, using reliable manuscripts and printed sources.
This underscores the importance of editorial work in fiqh research.
5
Apply to research
When researching a Hanafi ruling, a mufti or student would consult these commentaries to trace the evidence chain. For instance, al-Tahawi's Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (entry 185) is crucial for hadith-based arguments. Knowing which commentaries exist and their format (manuscript/printed) helps in planning research.
Manuscripts may contain unique readings not found in printed editions.

Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is a list of sources (مصادر) used in the critical edition of Al-Lubab (the commentary) and the matn (original text of Al-Quduri). It appears at the end of the book's introduction. The sources range from early Hanafi works to later commentaries and glosses. The list is numbered from 177 to 191, but there is a brief interruption ('-1A') which may be a manuscript reference. The sources include prominent Hanafi scholars such as al-Dardir, al-Harawi, al-Jassas, al-Uzjandi, al-Bukhari, al-Samarqandi, al-Tahawi, al-Buhuti, al-Kashghari, al-Halabi, al-Laknawi, and Tashkubri Zada. The list also includes modern editions and dissertations. This bibliography is essential for researchers to verify the texts used in the edition.

Key Terms
شرح (sharh): A commentary or exposition on a base text (matn).
مختصر (mukhtasar): An abridgment or summary of a larger fiqh work.
حاشية (hashiyah): A gloss or marginal commentary written on the margins of a sharh or matn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The critical edition's bibliography is a gateway to the Hanafi tradition — each entry represents a scholarly effort to preserve and transmit fiqh through generations.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Reading a Hanafi Fiqh Bibliography: The Sources of Al-Lubab
Bibliography of sources used in a critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize the sources listed in a Hanafi fiqh critical edition bibliography (manuscripts, commentaries, hadith collections, biographical works) and explain their role in textual verification.

Core Idea
A critical edition of a classical fiqh text depends on a chain of reliable sources — manuscripts, commentaries, and supporting works — each with its own authority.

This passage is a bibliography from the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh commentary. The list may look like a dry catalog, but it represents the scholarly apparatus that ensures the text is accurate and trustworthy. Understanding this bibliography is a first step in evaluating the quality of any critical edition you use in your studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose
Read the heading 'مصادر تحقيق اللباب والقدوري' (Sources for the critical edition of Al-Lubab and Al-Quduri). Recognize that this is not a list of legal rulings, but a list of works consulted by the editor to establish the correct text.
The bibliography is part of the editorial apparatus, not the fiqh content.
2
Categorize each entry
Go through entries 184–198 and sort them into categories: manuscripts (e.g., entry 184), published commentaries (e.g., 185, 186, 187), hadith collections (e.g., 194, 195), biographical works (e.g., 189, 197, 198), and modern editions or studies (e.g., 190, 196).
Note the diversity: fiqh, hadith, history, language.
3
Assess the temporal range
Note the dates of the authors: from al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH) to ‘Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah (d. 1417 AH). This shows the editor used sources spanning over a millennium, from early authorities to contemporary scholars.
The range indicates a thorough critical method.
4
Evaluate the relevance of each type
Consider why each category is important. Manuscripts provide direct textual evidence. Commentaries explain difficult passages and transmit variant readings. Hadith collections verify proofs. Biographical works confirm the reliability of authors cited in the text.
Each category contributes to the overall authority of the edition.

Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography of sources used by the editor (Sa'id Bakdash) in his critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri. It lists classical Hanafi works, hadith collections, biographical dictionaries, and modern editions. The list begins with a manuscript of Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Khatli (d. 600 AH) and includes Tahawi's Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar, which is essential for understanding Hanafi proofs. Also noted are later Hanafi commentaries like al-Halabi's Ghunyat al-Mutamalli, al-Laknawi's Sharh al-Hidayah, and biographical works such as al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyyah. The inclusion of Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim indicates reliance on primary hadith sources. This bibliography demonstrates the meticulous scholarly apparatus required for a reliable edition of a classical fiqh text.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The title of the commentary on Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar; literally 'the core' or 'the essence'.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh.
مخطوط (makhṭūṭ): Manuscript; handwritten copy, often the earliest form of a text.

Key Takeaway
A critical edition's bibliography is a scholarly tool that documents the textual chain and supports the edition's authority — learn to read it as part of evaluating any fiqh text.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Reading a Critical Edition's Bibliography: The Sources Behind Al-Lubab
List of references for the critical edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize the types of sources listed in a Hanafi fiqh edition's bibliography and explain how each type supports the editor's work.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the scholarly chain and the editor's methodological choices.

This lesson examines the bibliography from the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri. While not containing legal rulings, this section is vital for understanding how the editor reconstructed the text. You will learn to read such lists as evidence of scholarly practice.

Guided Path
1
Locate the section heading
Find the Arabic heading 'مصادر تحقيق اللباب والقدوري' and understand that it means 'Sources for the edition of Al-Lubab and Al-Quduri'. This tells you the editor is listing the references used.
The numbers indicate this is a continuation from previous pages.
2
Categorize entries by genre
Group the entries into categories: lexicons (e.g., al-Qamus al-Muhit), hadith works (e.g., Qawa'id fi 'Ulum al-Hadith), fiqh manuals (e.g., al-Qawanin al-Fiqhiyyah), biographical dictionaries (e.g., al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah), and manuscript catalogs (e.g., Fihris Makhtutat Dar al-Kutub al-Zahiriyyah).
Each genre serves a different purpose in the edition.
3
Analyze the contribution of each genre
For each genre, consider how it aids the editor: lexicons help define terms, hadith works authenticate prophetic traditions, fiqh manuals provide comparative rulings, biographies identify authors, and catalogs locate manuscripts.
This reveals the editor's comprehensive approach.
4
Examine the range of editions
Notice the diversity of publishers, dates, and locations (e.g., Karachi, Damascus, Beirut). This shows the editor consulted both classical and modern sources from various regions.
Geographic spread suggests access to multiple manuscript traditions.
5
Assess the scholarly rigor
The inclusion of multiple manuscript catalogs (e.g., Fihris al-Shamil, Fihris al-Zahiriyyah) and reference works indicates a thorough methodology. Missing such tools might reduce confidence in the edition.
This bibliography itself is a mark of academic transparency.

٢٣٩- القول البديع في الصلاة على الحبيب الشفيع ، للسخاوي محمد بن عبد الرحمن، ت ۹۰۲هـ ، تحقيق محمد عوامة، مؤسسة الريان، ط١٤٢٢/١هـ.
٢٤٠ - الكاشف في معرفة من له رواية في الكتب الستة، ومعه حاشية سبط ابن العجمي على الكاشف للذهبي محمد بن أحمد، ت ٧٤٨هـ، تحقيق محمد عوامة دار ،القبلة جدة، ط ١ / ١٤١٣هـ + ط١٤٣٠/٢هـ، دار اليسر، المدينة المنورة.
٢٤١ - كشاف اصطلاحات الفنون للتهانوي محمد علي بن علي الفاروقي، ت ۱۱۹۱ هـ ، الناشر سهيل أكيدمي، لاهور، باكستان، ط١٤١٣/١هـ.
٢٤٢ - كشف الأسرار شرح أصول البزدوي (علي بن محمد، ت ٤٨٢هـ)، علاء الدين البخاري عبد العزيز بن أحمد، ت ٧٣٠هـ، دار الكتاب الإسلامي، القاهرة.

Commentary
This is a bibliography section from the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri. It lists the sources consulted by the editor, covering Hanafi fiqh works, biographical dictionaries (tarajim), hadith sciences, lexicons, and manuscript catalogs. Each entry includes the author, title, editor, publisher, and publication details. Students should note that such bibliographies are standard in academic editions to provide transparency about the sources used. The list ranges from classical works to modern research tools, reflecting the editor's thorough methodology. The numbering (229-242) indicates this is a continuation from previous pages. This section does not contain legal rulings but rather documents the scholarly apparatus of the edition.

Key Terms
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical edition of a classical manuscript, involving verification of the text and documentation of sources.
مخطوطات (makhtutat): Manuscripts; handwritten copies of books before the printing press.
فهارس (faharis): Catalogs or indices; in this context, catalogs of manuscripts or of books in print.
تراجم (tarajim): Biographical entries; works that compile biographies of scholars (e.g., al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It contains the biography of the author of Al-Lubab.
D) It is an index of Quranic verses cited in the text.

Key Takeaway
A critical edition's bibliography is a scholarly tool that documents the sources used, ensuring transparency and allowing readers to verify the editor's work.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Navigating the Critical Edition Bibliography: The Sources Behind Al-Lubab
Bibliography list of 15 reference works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each component of a scholarly source entry (author, death date, editor, publisher) and assess the significance of a cited work for Hanafi fiqh research.

Core Idea
A scholarly edition's bibliography is your roadmap to the authority chain of the text.

This passage is not fiqh itself—it is the apparatus that tells you which editions and commentaries the editor used. Understanding this list trains you to evaluate the reliability of the edition you are reading and to trace the transmission of Hanafi knowledge. Each entry is a door to a classical work that shaped the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and author
Read the full title (e.g., Kashf al-Ilbas) and the author's name (e.g., al-Maydani al-Ghunaimi). This tells you which work is being cited.
Some titles have alternative names indicated by an equals sign (=), e.g., al-Kifaya = Fath al-Qadir.
2
Note the death date
The abbreviation 'ت' followed by a Hijri year gives the author's death date. This dates the work and helps assess its authority.
Earlier death dates often indicate more foundational texts.
3
Check publication status
Look for 'مخطوط' (manuscript) or printed details (publisher, place, edition). Manuscripts require further verification.
Printed editions include editor names, which show modern scholarly involvement.
4
Note editor and publisher
The editor (tahqiq) is the modern scholar who prepared the edition. The publisher and edition year indicate availability and quality.
Dār al-Ma‘rifa, al-Maktab al-Islamī, etc., are well-known publishers in the field.
5
Interpret cross-references
Some entries state that a work is equivalent to another (e.g., no. 249: 'Kanz al-Daqā’iq = al-Bahr al-Rā’iq'). This links commentaries to base texts.
Cross-references save time when you know one of the titles.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography of sources used in the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri. It lists 15 reference works (numbered 243-257) with full bibliographic details: author, death date, editor, publisher, place, and edition. These works include biographies, hadith terminologies, fiqh commentaries, and language dictionaries. The section is part of the editor's apparatus and provides transparency about the sources relied upon for the edition. Each entry follows a consistent format: number, title, author, death date (t), editor (tahqiq), publisher and place, and edition year. Some entries include cross-references to other works (e.g., no. 248 = Fath al-Qadir, no. 249 = al-Bahr al-Ra'iq). This is typical front matter for a scholarly edition of a classic Hanafi fiqh text.

Key Terms
مصادر تحقيق (masadir tahqiq): Sources used for the critical edition of a text.
ت (t): Abbreviation for 'توفي' (died) followed by the Hijri death year of the author.
ط (t): Abbreviation for 'طبعة' (edition) followed by the edition number and year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Hanafi Bibliography: Key Sources for Studying al-Quduri
Lists references used in the critical edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify five key classical Hanafi sources listed in the bibliography and explain their importance for fiqh studies.

Core Idea
A critical edition of a fiqh text relies on a diverse array of classical manuscripts and commentaries.

This passage is a bibliography (front matter) from the critical edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. Although it contains no legal rulings, it offers a window into the scholarly apparatus that underpins reliable fiqh study. Understanding these sources helps you navigate the Hanafi textual tradition and assess the authority of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of works
Scan the list and note categories: commentaries (e.g., al-Lubab), comprehensive fiqh works (al-Mabsut), hadith compilations (Majma' al-Zawa'id), language dictionaries (Lisan al-Arab), and biographical works (al-Kawakib al-Sa'ira).
This shows the interdisciplinary nature of fiqh scholarship.
2
Note authors and death dates
Each entry includes the author's name and death date (e.g., al-Sarakhsi d. 483 AH). Arrange them chronologically to see the development of the Hanafi school.
Al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut is a foundational text of the school.
3
Relate sources to their function
For each source, ask: what role does it play? Al-Mabsut provides detailed proofs; Lisan al-Arab clarifies linguistic meanings; Majma' al-Zawa'id gathers hadiths. This helps you know where to look for specific information.
The editor used these to verify and correct the text of al-Quduri.
4
Distinguish printed editions from manuscripts
Some entries are marked 'manuscript' (e.g., al-Lubab itself), indicating the editor worked directly from handwritten copies. Others are printed editions with publication details.
Manuscripts often have textual variants that affect the ruling.
5
Recognize the range of madhhabs and disciplines
The list includes works from other schools (e.g., al-Majmu' by al-Nawawi is Shafi'i) and non-fiqh disciplines. This reflects the comprehensive approach of critical edition.
Hanafi editors use Shafi'i works for hadith verification and linguistic accuracy.

-٢٥٨ المجتبى (شرح مختصر القدوري) للزاهدي نجم الدين مختار بن محمود، ت ٦٥٨هـ، (مخطوط).
٢٥٩ - مجمع الأمثال للنيسابوري الميداني أحمد بن محمد، ت ٥١٨هـ، تحقيق محمد محيي الدين عبد الحميد، المكتبة العصرية، بیروت، ١٤١٣هـ.
٢٦٠ - مجمع الأنهر شرح ملتقى الأبحر الإبراهيم بن محمد الحلبي)، لداماد أفندي عبد الرحمن محمد بن سليمان، ت ۱۰۷۸هـ، (ومعه الدر المنتقى في شرح الملتقى للحصكفي)، صورة عن الطبعة العثمانية سنة ١٣١٧هـ، تصوير دار إحياء التراث العربي، بيروت.
٢٦١ - مجمع البحرين وملتقى النيرين (النَّهْرَيْن) (جَمَع فيه بين القدوري ومنظومة النسفي)، لابن الساعاتي أحمد بن علي، ت ٦٩٤هـ، تحقيق إلياس ،قبلان دار الكتب العلمية، بيروت، ط١٤٢٦/١هـ.
-٢٦٢ مجمع الزوائد ومنبع الفوائد، الهيثمي نور الدين علي بن أبي بكر، ت ۸۰۷ هـ ، دار الكتاب العربي، بيروت، ط ۲ .
٢٦٣ - المجموع شرح المهذب النووي يحيى بـن شــرف ، ت ٦٧٦هـ ، دار الفكر، بيروت، تكملة مع تقي الدين السبكي علي بن عبد الكافي، ت ٧٥٦ هـ ( ج ١١ + ج ١٢) ، وتكملة محمد نجيب المطيعي، ت ١٤٠٦هـ ، (ج ١٣ - ج ٢٠).

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (front matter) listing the sources used in the critical edition of the Hanafi fiqh texts al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. The editor has drawn on a wide range of classical and later works, including the foundational Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi, the linguistic authority Lisan al-Arab, hadith collections like Majma' al-Zawa'id, and numerous commentaries and manuscripts. The list demonstrates the scholarly apparatus required for producing a reliable edition of a medieval fiqh text. The references are numbered and include author names, death dates, publication details, and manuscript status. This section does not contain any legal rulings but rather shows the textual foundation upon which the edition rests.

Key Terms
مصادر تحقيق (masadir tahqiq): Sources used for the critical edition
اللباب شرح الكتاب (al-Lubab Sharh al-Kitab): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Yazdi
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH)
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): A comprehensive Hanafi legal compendium by al-Sarakhsi

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Navigating the Sources of a Hanafi Critical Edition: A Bibliography Lesson
Listing of references in a critical edition bibliography

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of a Hanafi fiqh source reference (author, death date, editor, publication) and classify listed works as manuscripts, printed commentaries, or modern studies.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography is a map of the scholarly tradition – each entry tells you the authority, reliability, and era of a source.

This passage is the bibliography (مصادر تحقيق) from the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It lists 13 works (from 258 to 270) that the editor used. While not a legal text itself, understanding this list teaches you how Hanafi scholars cite their sources and what works are considered authoritative. You'll learn to parse entries like a research scholar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entry number and title
Each entry starts with a number (e.g., 258) followed by the Arabic title. Write down the full title as it appears, noting any significant terms like 'شرح' (commentary) or 'مختصر' (abridgment).
Titles often indicate the genre: e.g., 'مجمع الأنهر' is a fiqh commentary.
2
Locate the author and his death date
After the title, find the author's name. The death date (ت followed by the year AH) tells you the historical layer. For example, 'ت ٦٥٨هـ' for al-Zahidi indicates a 7th-century Hanafi scholar.
The death date is crucial for dating the work relative to other sources.
3
Check for editor and publication details
Modern editions mention 'تحقيق' (edited by) and the publisher, place, and edition year. Manuscripts are marked 'مخطوط' (manuscript). For example, entry 258 is a manuscript, while entry 259 is a printed book.
Manuscripts are less accessible; printed editions have a specific edition and year.
4
Classify the type of work
Determine the genre: is it a Hanafi fiqh commentary (e.g., 'المجتبى', 'مجمع الأنهر'), a hadith collection (e.g., 'مجمع الزوائد'), a tafsir (e.g., 'المحرر الوجيز'), a dictionary (e.g., 'مختار الصحاح'), or a modern academic study (e.g., 'المذهب الحنفي')?
Some works are from other madhhabs, like 'المجموع' (Shafi'i) or 'المحلى' (Dhahiri).
5
Assess its relevance to Hanafi fiqh
Ask: does this work directly comment on al-Quduri? Is it a core Hanafi reference? Or is it a source of hadith or language used to support fiqh arguments? This helps you understand why the editor included it.
The editor likely used a mix of primary Hanafi texts and supporting works from other disciplines.

Commentary
This passage is the bibliography (مصادر تحقيق) of the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It lists the works consulted by the editor, arranged numerically from 258 to 270 (the numbering continues from previous pages). Each entry gives the title, author, death date (ت), and publication details. The list includes commentaries on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar (like al-Mujtaba and Majma' al-Bahrayn), major Hanafi fiqh works (like Majma' al-Anhur), hadith collections (Majma' al-Zawa'id), Shafi'i fiqh (al-Majmu'), tafsir (al-Muharrar al-Wajiz), and modern studies on the Hanafi madhhab. This demonstrates the scholarly rigor of the edition, drawing from manuscripts, printed works, and academic theses.

Key Terms
المجتبى (al-Mujtabā): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Zahidi, used as a manuscript source.
مجمع الأنهر (Majma‘ al-Anhur): A famous Hanafi fiqh commentary on Multaqa al-Abhar by Damad Afandi.
مجمع البحرين (Majma‘ al-Bahrayn): A work that combines al-Quduri's Mukhtasar with al-Nasafi's poem, by Ibn al-Sa'ati.
مختصر الطحاوي (Mukhtasar al-Ṭaḥāwī): An early Hanafi fiqh compendium by al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH).

Reading the Bibliography of al-Lubab: A Hanafi Source Guide
Bibliography of sources for critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of sources (hadith, fiqh commentary, biographical) used in a critical edition of a Hanafi text and explain their contribution to verifying the text's authenticity.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the scholarly chain: hadith, fiqh, and modern sources anchor the text.

This passage is a bibliography from the critical edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri by Sa'id Bakdash. It lists 15 sources (entries 271-286) used to verify the text. As a Hanafi student, understanding these sources gives you insight into the scholarly methodology behind the edition and helps you gauge the reliability of the text you are studying.

Guided Path
1
Identify source categories
Scan the list and group entries into categories: hadith collections (e.g., Musannaf, Musnad), fiqh commentaries (e.g., Maraqi al-Falah), and modern studies (e.g., Masha'ikh Balkh).
This helps appreciate the breadth of evidence used.
2
Note the authors and their madhhab
Many authors are Hanafi (e.g., al-Shurunbulali, Mulla 'Ali al-Qari) or widely respected in hadith (e.g., Ibn Abi Shayba). Recognize their reliability for Hanafi fiqh.
A Hanafi edition often prioritizes Hanafi authors for fiqh sources.
3
Understand the editor's method
The editor used multiple editions and manuscripts (e.g., entry 274 mentions a manuscript). This shows critical textual work.
Look for clues like 'manuscript' or multiple publishers.

مصادر تحقيق اللباب والقدوري
۲۷۱ - المراسيل، لأبي داود سليمان بن الأشعث، ت٢٧٥هـ، تحقيق شعيب الأرناؤط ، ط ١٤٠٨/١ هـ، مؤسسة الرسالة، بيروت.
۲۷۲ - مراقي الفلاح شرح نور الإيضاح للشرنبلالي حسن بن عمار، ت ١٠٦٩هـ ، دار المعرفة، بيروت.
۲۷۳ - مرقاة المفاتيح شرح مشكاة المصابيح ملا علي القاري ـ ١٠١٤هـ مكتبة الإمدادية، ملتان، باكستان.
٢٧٤ - المسائل البهيَّة الزكيَّة على الاثني عشرية، للشرنبلالي حسن بن عمار، ت ١٠٦٩هـ، (مخطوط).
٢٧٥- المسالك في المناسك ، للكرماني محمد بن مكرم، ت ٥٩٧هـ، تحقيق د/ سعود بن إبراهيم الشريم دار البشائر الإسلامية، بيروت، ط١٤٢٤/١هـ.
٢٧٦- المستدرك على الصحيحين، محمد بن عبد الله النيسابوري، ت ٤٠٥ هـ ، دار الكتاب العربي، بيروت.
۲۷۷- مسند أبي داود الطيالسي سليمان بن داود، ت٢٠٤هـ، تحقيق محمد عبد المحسن التركي، دار هجر القاهرة، ط١٤١٩/١هـ + دار الكتاب اللبناني، بيروت.
۲۷۸- مسند أبي يعلى الموصلي، أحمد بن علي، ت ٣٠٧هـ، تحقيق حسین أسد، دار المأمون للتراث، دمشق.
٢٧٩- مسند الإمام أبي حنيفة مع شرحه : تنسيق النظام، للسنبهلي، ت ١٣٠٥هـ)، النعمان بن ثابت ت ١٥٠ هـ ، طبعة حجرية، مير محمد كتب خانة، كراتشي، باكستان.
۲۸۰ - مسند الإمام أبي حنيفة (مع شرحه لملا علي القاري، ت ١٠١٤هـ)، النعمان بن ثابت، ت ١٥٠ هـ ، دار الكتب العلمية، بيروت، ١٤٠٥/١هـ.
۲۸۱ - مسند الإمام أحمد بن حنبل، ت ٢٤١ هـ، المكتـب الإسلامي، بيروت، ودار صادر، بیروت، تحقيق أحمد شاكر، ط ١٣٦٨/٣هـ.
۲۸۲ - مسند الإمام الشافعي، محمد بن إدريس، ت ٢٠٤هـ، دار الكتب العلمية، بيروت، ط١٤٠٠/١هـ.
۲۸۳ - مشايخ بلخ من الحنفية، وما انفردوا به من المسائل الفقهية، د/ محمد أحمد بن المدرس ( رسالة دكتوراه، عام ١٣٩٧هـ)، طبع وزارة الأوقاف العراق.
٢٨٤ - المصباح المنير في غريب الشرح الكبير، للرافعي، محمد المقري الفيومي، ت ٧٧٠ هـ.
٢٨٥ - المصنف في الأحاديث والآثار، أبو بكر عبد الله بن محمد بن أبي شيبة، ت ٢٣٥ هـ، الدار السلفية ، ط ۲/ ۱۳۹۹ هـ + ط بتحقيق محمد عوامة دار ،القبلة جدة، ط١٤٢٧/١هـ.
٢٨٦ - المصنف، عبد الرزاق بن همام الصنعاني، ت ٢١١ هـ، تحقيق حبيب الرحمن الأعظمي، ط ۱ / ۱۳۹۰ هـ، تصوير المكتـب الإسلامي، بيروت.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography listing the sources consulted by the editor (Sa'id Bakdash) in his critical edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It spans from entry 271 to 286, covering key Hanafi and general Islamic works. The list includes hadith collections (Marasil, Musannaf, Mustadrak), fiqh commentaries (Maraqi al-Falah, Mirqat al-Mafatih), and specialized Hanafi studies (Masha'ikh Balkh). Each entry provides author, death date, editor, publisher, and edition. This demonstrates the breadth of classical and modern scholarship used to verify the text of al-Lubab. For students of Hanafi fiqh, knowing these sources is important for understanding the authority and methodology behind the edition.

Key Terms
مراقي الفلاح (Maraqi al-Falah): A Hanafi fiqh commentary by al-Shurunbulali on Nur al-Idah, covering acts of worship and transactions.
مسند الإمام أبي حنيفة (Musnad al-Imam Abi Hanifah): A collection of hadith narrated by Abu Hanifah, compiled by later scholars.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Source Base of Hanafi Fiqh: The Bibliography of Al-Lubab
List of manuscripts and printed works cited by the editor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major hadith collections and reference works cited in the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri and explain their relevance to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
The editor's bibliography reveals the scholarly network of hadith, fiqh, and biography that underpins the Hanafi tradition.

A critical edition is only as strong as the sources it draws upon. The bibliography at the end of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri lists the manuscripts and printed works that the editor consulted to verify the text and its legal content. This lesson walks you through those sources, focusing on the hadith collections that are central to Hanafi istidlal. Understanding this list will help you appreciate how a modern scholar reconstructs the classical Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the sources
Group the entries into categories: hadith collections (Musnad, Musannaf, Mu'jam), fiqh commentaries, biographical dictionaries, and modern works (theses, dictionaries). This helps see the range of material used.
Most entries are hadith collections, reflecting the need to verify prophetic reports and companion sayings (athar) that Al-Quduri and Al-Maydani cite.
2
Identify the Hanafi-specific sources
Look for the Musnad of Imam Abu Hanifa (entry 280) and the work on Hanafi scholars of Balkh (entry 283). These are directly tied to the Hanafi school and its early development.
The Musnad of Abu Hanifa, with the commentary of Mulla 'Ali al-Qari, is a key source for transmitting the Imam's own hadith methodology.
3
Note the reliance on classical hadith collections
The list includes Musnad Ahmad, Musnad al-Shafi'i, and the Musannafs of Ibn Abi Shaybah and 'Abd al-Razzaq. These are not Hanafi-specific but are used by all madhahib. The editor uses them to cross-check narrations cited in the Sharh.
The Musannaf works are arranged by fiqh topics, making them especially useful for legal verification.
4
Observe the geographical and temporal range
Sources range from early (d. 150 AH, Abu Hanifa) to later (d. 1397 AH, al-Banuri). The list also includes modern editions and a PhD thesis, showing that the editor incorporates both classical manuscripts and contemporary scholarship.
This breadth ensures the edition is authoritative and up-to-date.
5
Understand the purpose of the bibliography
The bibliography serves as a guarantee of scholarly rigor. By listing all sources, the editor enables readers to verify the text and encourages further research. It also demonstrates the interconnectedness of hadith, fiqh, and biography in Hanafi studies.
A well-prepared bibliography is a hallmark of a critical edition.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography, listing the primary and secondary sources used by the editor in preparing the critical edition of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri. It includes key hadith collections (Musnads, Musannafs), fiqh works, biographical dictionaries, and other reference works. The list reflects the thoroughness of the edition, drawing on sources from various Islamic disciplines. Notably, the Musnad of Imam Abu Hanifa is included, which is of particular importance to the Hanafi school, and the commentary by Mulla 'Ali al-Qari is a standard reference. The bibliography also mentions a thesis on the Hanafi scholars of Balkh, indicating regional contributions to the madhhab. The editor relies on both early manuscripts and modern printed editions, demonstrating a careful scholarly method.

Key Terms
مسند (musnad): A type of hadith collection arranged by the name of the companion who narrated the hadith, not by topic.
مصنف (musannaf): A hadith collection arranged by legal topic (e.g., taharah, salah, etc.), often including both marfu' and mawquf narrations.
معجم (mu'jam): A dictionary or biographical dictionary, often arranged alphabetically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Sources Behind a Critical Edition of a Hanafi Text (al-Lubab and al-Quduri)
List of reference works used in the critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the categories of sources (commentaries, hadith works, biographical dictionaries, etc.) listed in a critical edition of a Hanafi fiqh text and explain why each category is important for textual verification.

Core Idea
A critical edition's bibliography reveals the scholarly lineage and textual integrity of a Hanafi masterpiece.

This lesson introduces the bibliography appended to the critical edition of al-Lubab (a commentary on al-Quduri). While not a ruling, this list is a roadmap to the sources the editor used to establish the correct text. Understanding this list helps you appreciate the scholarly apparatus behind reliable fiqh texts and equips you to evaluate the authority of a given edition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main categories of sources
Scan the list and group entries into broad categories: Hanafi fiqh commentaries, hadith compilations, biographical works (tarajim), usul al-fiqh, Quranic sciences, and other reference works.
For example, al-Hidayah is a commentary, Nasb al-Rayah is a hadith work on al-Hidayah, and Nuzhat al-Khawatir is a biographical dictionary.
2
Note the authors and their madhhab affiliation
Most authors are Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Ayni, Ibn Abidin, al-Marghinani). Some are from other madhhabs (e.g., al-Shawkani, a Zahiri). This helps assess the breadth and potential cross-madhhab references.
Al-Shawkani's Nayl al-Awtar is a hadith-based fiqh work, not strictly Hanafi.
3
Recognize the purpose of each source
Understand whether a source is used to verify the matn (base text), provide sharh (commentary), cite hadith evidence, or correct transmission errors. The editor likely consulted multiple works for cross-verification.
Al-Nihaya fi Gharib al-Hadith helps clarify obscure hadith terms.
4
Assess the chronological range
The sources span from early (e.g., Ibn al-Athir, d. 606) to later (e.g., al-Kawthari, d. 1371) periods. This shows the editor's effort to use both classical and modern scholarly input.
Later works like al-Nukat al-Tarifah (al-Kawthari) engage with critiques against Abu Hanifa.
5
Note the edition and publication details
The bibliography includes publisher, edition year, and editor. This allows you to locate the same edition and verify the editor's own methodology.
Many works are printed by Dar Ihya' al-Turath or other academic publishers.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography appended by the critical editor, Said Bakdash, listing the sources he utilized in establishing the text of Al-Lubab by al-Maydani and its base text Al-Quduri. The list includes numerous classical works of Hanafi fiqh, usul al-fiqh, hadith, and biographies, demonstrating the scholarly apparatus behind the edition. Notable works include Al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, Al-Nihayah by Ibn al-Athir, and various commentaries and supercommentaries.

Key Terms
مصادر تحقيق (masadir tahqiq): List of reference sources used in the critical edition of a text.
شرح (sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).
تحقيق (tahqiq): Critical editing of a manuscript to produce a reliable published text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To provide a biography of al-Zayla'i

C) To list the chapters of al-Hidayah
D) To give a ruling on prayer times

Key Takeaway
The scholarly apparatus of a critical edition provides the intellectual foundation for studying a classical fiqh text.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: A Bibliographic Overview
Bibliographic listing of commentaries and scholarly works on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the most important commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain their role in Hanafi legal education.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the Hanafi primer; its 122+ commentaries form the backbone of the madhhab's scholarly tradition.

This passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab presents a list of commentaries and related works on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the foundational Hanafi fiqh primer. While this appears to be a simple catalog, it reveals the immense scholarly attention given to al-Quduri's text over centuries. Understanding this bibliography is key to navigating Hanafi source material and recognizing the hierarchy of commentaries used in study and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Recognize that Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) is the central primer being commented upon.
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is one of the earliest and most widespread Hanafi texts.
2
Distinguish types of works
The list includes commentaries (shuruh), glosses (hawashi), and independent works that incorporate or reorganize the Mukhtasar. Note the variety: some are large, some small, some are versified (Nazm).
Not every work is a direct commentary; some are expansions or combinations.
3
Identify prominent examples
Pay attention to well-known works like al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani and al-Lubab itself. These are cornerstone texts in the Hanafi curriculum.
Al-Hidayah is a commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, which itself combines al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
4
Understand the list's significance
The sheer number (122 works) shows the Mukhtasar's centrality. This bibliography helps students trace the chain of transmission and select the appropriate commentary for their level.
Many of these works are lost or only available in manuscript, but the list preserves their titles and authors.

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents from the front matter of a modern edition of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab. It outlines the study topics for the book's introduction and then lists 27 commentaries and related works on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, one of the most foundational texts in the Hanafi school. The author first discusses al-Quduri's methodology, sources, influence, manuscript variations, and editions. Then he catalogs 122 works based on the Mukhtasar, but here he lists 27 prominent ones, including the well-known al-Hidayah of al-Marghinani and al-Lubab itself. The list demonstrates the central role of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in Hanafi legal education and scholarship. Each entry names the author and often a brief description. This is a bibliographic overview, not a fiqh ruling, so no legal analysis is provided.

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri generated over 122 scholarly works, indicating its central role in the Hanafi tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Key Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: A Bibliographic Overview
Bibliographic list of Hanafi fiqh commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major commentaries and abridgments of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and state their authors and significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the root; Al-Hidayah, Al-Wafi, and Al-Kafi are its most influential offshoots.

This passage lists 45 works that build upon Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi text. Understanding this bibliography helps you navigate the tradition and know which commentaries are relied upon for study and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) is the concise manual that many later scholars commented on or summarized.
It is one of the earliest mukhtasarat in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Trace the most famous commentary lineage
Notice the chain: Mukhtasar al-Quduri → Bidayat al-Mubtadi (compiled by al-Marghinani) → Al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani's own commentary). Al-Hidayah is the most widely used reference.
Bidayat al-Mubtadi combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri with al-Jami' al-Saghir.
3
Identify the comprehensive works by al-Nasafi
Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi wrote Al-Wafi and then Al-Kafi Sharh al-Wafi. These are later authoritative commentaries.
Al-Nasafi's works are known for their clarity and wide acceptance.
4
Note the supplementary works
Some authors wrote supplements (Takmilah) or compiled works that combine al-Quduri with other texts, e.g., Majma' al-Bahrayn by Ibn al-Sa'ati.
These show how the Hanafi tradition expanded and cross-referenced.
5
Recognize the scholarly network
The list includes scholars from various regions (e.g., Zamakhshari, Sarakhsi, Nasafi) indicating the wide reach of al-Quduri's text.
Many of these works are still studied in traditional Hanafi curricula.

Commentary
This is a front-matter passage from the book Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, which is itself a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The passage lists 45 works (numbered 9 through 45) that are commentaries, abridgments, or related texts to the foundational Hanafi fiqh work Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Ahmad al-Quduri. The list includes major works such as Al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, Al-Wafi and Al-Kafi by al-Nasafi, and many others. It serves as a bibliography showing the extensive scholarly activity around al-Quduri's text, which is a staple of Hanafi fiqh study. The page numbers at the right indicate where these works can be found in the current book. This list is useful for students to know the key commentaries and their authors.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal manual by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh.
الهداية (Al-Hidayah): The famous commentary by al-Marghinani on his own Bidayat al-Mubtadi, widely used as a primary reference in Hanafi fiqh.
الوافي (Al-Wafi): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, often studied after al-Hidayah.
الكافي (Al-Kafi): Al-Nasafi's own commentary on his Al-Wafi, providing additional explanations and proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following works is a commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi by al-Marghinani?

C) Al-Kafi
D) Al-Mujtaba

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi tradition built a rich textual layer around Mukhtasar al-Quduri, with Al-Hidayah and Al-Nasafi's works as key milestones for study and fatwa.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Commentary Tradition on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
An inventory of commentaries on a foundational Hanafi text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify major commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain their significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the bedrock of Hanafi fiqh; its commentaries form a vast scholarly heritage.

Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a foundational text in the Hanafi madhhab, studied for centuries. The extensive commentary tradition—ranging from concise glosses to comprehensive expositions—reflects its central role. This lesson introduces you to a partial list of those commentaries, helping you understand the landscape of Hanafi fiqh literature and where to find further explanations of key rulings.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the base text
Identify Mukhtasar al-Quduri as the core matn (text) that generated these commentaries. Understand that it is a concise manual of Hanafi law.
The text is also known as Kitab al-Quduri.
2
Identify key commentators
Scan the list for well-known scholars such as al-Haddad (author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara al-Nayyira), al-Nasafi (Kanz al-Daqa'iq), and al-Halabi (Multaqa al-Abhar). Note their contributions.
3
Note works that combine multiple texts
Observe that some works like Multaqa al-Abhar integrate Mukhtasar al-Quduri with other major Hanafi texts (al-Mukhtar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Wiqaya). This shows efforts to harmonize multiple authoritative sources.
Such works are useful for comparative study.
4
Recognize unknowns as areas for research
Several entries are marked ‘majhul’ (unknown author). Recognize that the commentary tradition is vast and not all works have survived or been identified. This opens possibilities for historical research.

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of a bibliography listing commentaries and related works on Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a seminal text in the Hanafi madhhab. The list includes titles such as Kanz al-Daqa'iq by al-Nasafi, multiple commentaries titled Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by various scholars, and specialized works like al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara al-Nayyira by al-Haddad. Notably, some entries are marked as 'majhul' (unknown author), indicating lost or obscure works. The list also includes works that combine multiple texts, such as Multaqa al-Abhar, which integrates Mukhtasar al-Quduri with other key Hanafi texts. This inventory serves as a valuable resource for students and researchers tracking the transmission and commentary tradition of al-Quduri's work.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Quduri, widely studied and commented upon.
شرح (Sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).
مجهول (Majhul): Unknown author; used in bibliographies when the author of a work is not identified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri has been extensively commented upon; knowing these works helps navigate Hanafi fiqh literature.
